		<date>2002-10-21</date>
		<username>(bsmith5552@rogers.com)</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>Captivating Drama with Superb Acting!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>When first approaching this movie I thought, oh no, not another alien comes to earth movie. But much to my surprise, it turned out to be a captivating drama highlighted by the superb acting of the film's two stars Kevin Spacey and Jeff Bridges. Spacey plays "Prot" a man who seemingly "appears" in Grand Central Station (without his razor). When he tries to help a mugging victim, he identifies himself to police as a visitor from a far away planet named K-Pax. Naturally the police assume he is unbalanced and send him to a mental facility. Later he is sent to psychiatrist Dr. Mark Powell (Bridges) for an evaluation. In the course of their conversations Prot gives convincing arguments to support his claim that he is an alien. He even impresses some world class scientists with his knowledge of his "home" galaxy, which is apparently only known to few. Back in the mental facility he is having a positive effect on the lives of several of the other patients. He gives them hope by convincing them that they can overcome their various handicaps. Meanwhile Dr. Powell is trying to unravel the mystery. He finds some of the answers by hypnotizing Prot and probing his past. Yet at the end of the film we are still left wondering, was this guy really who he said he was. Director Iain Softly skillfully keeps the viewer's interest by not letting to much of the cat out of the bag at a time. He is aided by an outstanding performance by Kevin Spacey, who is so convincing that you really believe his sincerity. He is particularly good during the hypnotic sequences. Jeff Bridges plays very well against Spacey as the concerned psychiatrist. Others in the cast include Mary McCormack as Bridges' wife, Alfre Woodard as his boss and David Patrick Kelly and Saul Williams as Howie and Ernie, two of the mental patients that Prot helps. A riveting movie.</fullReview>
	</review>
	<review>
		<date>2002-10-14</date>
		<username>sddavis63 (revsdd@gmail.com)</username>
		<score>0.9</score>
		<shortDescription>Excellent Movie With Excellent Performances</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I have to admit that I was very pleasantly surprised by this movie. I had expected it to be a fairly hokey sci-fi adventure, and instead I discovered it to be a truly thought-provoking adventure that certainly kept me guessing all the way through about the real identity of Prot - and that still has me guessing even after I've seen the movie. That to me is the mark of a truly good movie. Usually I'm left somewhat empty by loose ends that aren't tied up; I like a certain degree of closure to a movie. In this case, though, the uncertainty seems appropriate and added to the overall high quality of the movie.The performances were of generally high quality. I've always thought that Kevin Spacey was a decent enough actor - albeit one who in my opinion has not always chosen the best vehicles to showcase his talents and who has fallen into a certain pattern of playing emotionally challenged characters (His work in "The Shipping News" and "American Beauty" come to mind as examples.) The character of Prot certainly has elements of that pattern (particularly as the movie progresses) but Prot is also a very different kind of character for Spacey, and I thought that he handled the challenges of basically playing two characters in one (I won't say any more about that so as not to spoil anything) extremely well. Jeff Bridges also surprised me with what I thought was one of the better performances I have ever seen him offer as Dr. Powell, the psychiatrist charged with sorting out the mystery surrounding Prot.The story is well written, well developed and very interesting. As I said, it has the ability to keep the viewer guessing all the way through and beyond. The only real weakness to the story comes at the very beginning. I wasn't entirely sure why it was that Prot would have been taken into custody at the train station. True, the police originally thought he had mugged the old lady, but in truth he hadn't done anything, there were witnesses saying that he hadn't done anything and the old lady confirmed that he hadn't done anything. Why take him into custody? Because he had caused no trouble? Sure, he was a bit unusual and had no I.D. but - this is New York City for goodness' sake! That's reason to put someone into a psych ward? Struck me as a bit far-fetched, but it was the only real weakness I could see in an otherwise superb story.9/10</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>This Film Is Generally Misunderstood</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Very few people I know who have seen K-PAX, understood or liked it, when, in my opinion, it is the best film to come out of Hollywood since Forrest Gump. The concept behind K-PAX is simple. A man suffers a horrible and overwhelming loss, one his mind refuses to accept. He, in course, tries to take his own life. Instead he survives, but has literally become another person. Prot from the planet K-PAX. This is not a case of split personality, Prot and Robert Porter are two very different beings. You witness Prot preform things in this film that are beyond all human capability, yet, it seems to never explain why or how. THAT is when you, the viewer, must use your greatest resourses, imagination and common sense. Prot can see Ultra-Violet light, he can come and go as he pleases. HOW is this possible if he were once as human as you or I? Medical Science has proven that we only use about 10% of our brain for everything from memory to bodily functions. It is my opinion that Robert Porter awoke after trying to drown himself, with the ability to use 100% of his brain capacity. And no one knows exactly what we would capable of if we could all tap into 90% of un-used brain matter. Prot WAS an Alien, one from Earth! The only person alive with the ability to use all of his brain. Let us not forget Bess. After nearly five years of being Prot, Robert Porter wanted out, he wanted to face and deal with his loss, and, he did, after doing so he passed his gift to sweet little Bess and she vanished without a trace. This film had OSCAR written all over it, but the Academy overlooked it. I highly recommend this film to anyone who dares to dream and uses their imagination. Kevin Spacey and Jeff Bridges are magnificent, as is this film.</fullReview>

		<date>2002-06-14</date>
		<username>kep315</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Misnomer about K-Pax being remake</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I have to correct what a couple of people have said about "K-Pax" being a remake of "Hombre mirando al sudeste" (AKA "Man Facing Southeast") Yes, the plot line is similar. In both, a man claiming he is an alien ends up in a mental hospital, where a doctor tries to cure him of his delusion. But NO, it is not a remake. "K-Pax" is based upon the novel of the same name by Gene Brewster. There is a notice on Brewster's own website which reads: "A NOTE FROM THE AUTHOR ABOUT MAN FACING SOUTHEAST: Universal Pictures has recently been sued by the owner of the English-language rights to MFSE. I first learned about this Argentinian film five years after I'd written K-PAX. Any similarity in plotline between the two is, therefore, purely coincidental." Hope this clears up any confusion.</fullReview>
	</review>

	<review>
		<date>2002-05-22</date>
		<username>Jon Hartley (hockeyguy9)</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>A Very Unique Story With Imagination</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>K-PAX is about a mysterious stranger who claims to be from another planet. He goes to help a lady who has been mugged, and when the police come, they question him...of course, his deadpan expression as he says he's from the planet "K-PAX" lands him in the mental ward.From there, Prot (Kevin Spacey) enters an interesting doctor-patient relationship with Dr. Mark Powell (Jeff Bridges), which is really the heart of the film. Prot's revelations about life on the idealistic planet he's "from" helps others, including Powell and the other patients, make changes in their own lives. From their we get the main subplots of the film.About half-way through, the story changes direction a bit as Powell finds a link between Prot and an actual human friend from Earth that Prot had. He investigates this and finds several surprises about this friend of Prot's, that ultimately leads to Powell once again doubting Prot's claims to be an alien. This leads to a conclusion that allows the viewer to decide for themselves exactly what Prot is all about, and where the truth lies.All in all, it's a very good film, especially since it stands out from the rest of the films we see these days as an imaginative and creative effort. Spacey is terrific, of course, especially during the hypnotism scenes which allow him to display his range a bit; since Prot himself is a bit subdued and straight-forward in his mannerisms. The dialogue is done quite well and Powell is a believable character in that he is very skeptical throughout, but begins to believe in Prot just as the viewer does. In a way, it's easy to see yourself in Powell's position throughout the film. The movie does lose a bit of steam once Powell starts investigating Prot's relationship with Robert Porter (Prot's human friend), but this does lead to the conclusion, which is thought-provoking and satisfying. The direction is done well by Iain Softley, as the theme is flashes of light and rays of light; the method in which Prot supposedly (I'll leave it up to you to believe him or not) travels between K-PAX and Earth. Well worth seeing. 8/10.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>Superior fusion of sci-fi and psychological mystery</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>K-Pax boasts fabulous performances, sensitive direction, a beautiful score and an intelligent script based on the wonderfully addictive book by Gene Brewer.It would be wrong to assume this movie is pure sci-fi. It works on many levels and addresses some deep psychological issues in a *very* moving way. The chemistry between patient and psychologist becomes more and more fascinating as the movie progresses and while the theme of trauma is addressed powerfully, it never overwhelms the viewer and is superbly offset by the cheeky character of prot, alongside the genuine concern of his therapist.I would give this movie ten, but for the fact that the wife and family of Dr. Powell are younger here than in the book, and this unfortunately sidesteps some deeper issues that are present in the text. Don't let this put you off, though. This is still a moving and intelligent movie that has an awful lot to offer. Direction is virtually flawless.The region 1 DVD is great too, with a good batch of extras including an audio commentary. Just a shame it doesn't really acknowledge the original author of the story, Gene Brewer.I would urge you to read the book if you enjoy this movie at all. It is brilliant and delves much deeper.Let's just hope they decide to make a sequel of Gene Brewer's superb follow-up, On a Beam of Light. The market for it will build and build.Highly recommended!</fullReview>

		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>One of those rare movies with a little piece of magic</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>In an absorbing and gentle way the story of a man who may or may not be what he seems is brilliantly brought to the screen. This is one of those priceless gems which every now and then bring back to the blase movie-buff a little piece of that magic they remember experiencing as a kid. Why is K-Pax so? That is the billion dollar question! The story itself is unusual, charming, intriguing, harrowing and yet somehow inspirational. It has no dazzeling effects, no pirotechnics, no specatular stunts or eye popping cgi, but what it does have are two leading actors who are absolutely at the top of their game. Completely natural, completely real. You know these guys. You've met them. By the end of the movie you feel as if they are your friends and all the way through you really care what happens. You empathise, you sympathise and the result is that piece of cinema magic that so often eludes even the most brilliant production. The direction is high quality, the cinematography is clear and crisp, the dialogue is natural and the supporting cast are superb. I won't go into the story which is in itself, superb. I will just say this is a rare jewel of a movie in which everything comes together in such a natural and unforced way that it doesn't end when the credits roll. It stays with you.Sheer class.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>a truly enigmatic and beautiful film</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>K-Pax, while coming off as trite at certain points, especially in Prot's last comments regarding the regeneration of the universe and the glorified notions of family, is still a fantastic movie. The art direction is flawless,drawing appropriate attention to aspects of life that we take for granted. The light refracting off a prism, a blue jay nesting on a tree etc. The biblical allusions relating Prot to the Messiah are of course evident, although, seen in its own individual light, there is much elegance in the tale being told here. The planet K Pax, is described by Prot to be a wonderfully beautiful environment, almost like an utopian society, and yet their immense intelligence and capacity to be so isolated from one another makes it seem almost cold. Like the Universe perhaps, there is really no telling which world one would prefer to live in. The miracle that is K Pax, or the mix and match jumble sale that is the Earth. Spacey's portrayal is fluid and perfect, though a little too much like his other roles, there is no telling where Spacey ends and Prot begins. And i am seriously wondering if he is starting to get typecast and should leave off such in-depth roles for a while.It is a movie that excites the senses, and fires the imagination. And never have I craved a fruit salad more!</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>K-Pax is a great vehicle for Kevin Spacey.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>K-Pax is a great vehicle for Kevin Spacey who plays Prot, a visitor from K-Pax, a planet orbiting a binary star system 1000 light-years away. Forced into the psychiatric hospital run-around for all the usual reasons, Prot becomes the pet project of a psychiatrist played by Jeff Bridges. Bridges' character then becomes wrapped-up in Prot's story and even more determined to discover his real identity as an ever-widening circle of people around him come to believe Prot is from K-Pax. An "outsider" fills this movie with interesting observations of humans and a touching story about all that matters in the universe is what you choose to do in this instant. Some themes are reminiscent of the recursive reality in which the movie 12 Monkeys revolves. Recommended.</fullReview>

		<date>2002-04-23</date>
		<username>(budasca)</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Brilliant movie</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Warning : Spoilers containedAs many of Kevin Spacey's movies, I think that K-Pax is a brilliant piece of cinematography. The movie not only impresses you by its atmosphere created by the music, the strange things happening, the lucidity and logic of the supposed alien character Prot, it also tries to respond to a few existentialist questions concerning our life on this planet.One of the keywords in this movie is "happiness"; almost all the characters in the movie are more or less unhappy from different reasons and, as everyone of us, they are trying to find their happiness. Seeing "the blue bird of happiness" creates a moment of exaltation for the patients, for a few moments they are content to live their life.A good way to reach happiness is founding a family, having a wife and kids; this idea is sustained many times in the movie: first of all by presenting Prot, the supposed alien identified by his name (PROT like Porter ROberT) and by his appearance with the character Robert Porter who lost his wife and daughter; although Prot does not directly express his regret for not having a family and considers normal that a k-paxian child should make his first steps in life learning from different people that are not his biological parents, you can feel his sadness for not having anyone waiting for him at home, not having a family and somebody who really cares for him. Mrs. Powell's remark `you don't know what you're missing' (when speaking about her family) is one of the only remarks in the entire movie remaining without a response from the logic `M. Know Everything' Prot.The only chance that Dr. Powell has to reconcile with his son can be understood in a more large sense; everybody has only one life, only one chance to live it and do the things right. This is a good reason for everyone to refuse being afraid of what could happen to him, idea which Ernie and Howie understood very well and got out of the hospital.Robert Porter, who could have left with his wife avoiding to become a `knocker' and to have his wife and daughter killed, had missed his chance 5 years ago; now he tries hardly to make the others happy or to teach them how to reach their happiness.The planet K-Pax has two suns and even if they only rise together once every 200 years, there should be more light on K-Pax than on Earth; but Prot wears sunglasses and says the reason is that the days on K-Pax are like the dawns on Earth. This lack of light expresses one more time the sadness of Prot (Robert Porter) who already missed his chance by losing his wife and daughter; he wears his glasses because he doesn't want to look at the light anymore, he stopped fighting. Prot has only about 150 years, so eventually he had never seen the two suns, he had never had light in his life as Robert Porter lost his father since he was a kid and then his wife and daughter. What Prot does, is though the opposite of the message transmitted to the others during the entire movie and most clearly in the end by the note left on the table near his sunglasses before leaving on K-Pax.The classic idea found in many other movies that people should enlarge their field of vision and learn to accept without eventually being afraid what they do not understand is expressed very well by Prot with his last words of a normal non-catatonic person : `I will accept the possibility that I am Robert Porter if you accept the possibility that I am from K-Pax'.The end of the movie gives no answer to the question `Is Prot or not from K-Pax?'; there is no answer because there should be no question.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<fullReview>This is an exceptional performance by Mr Spacey as a man in a psychiatric ward who claims to be from the planet K PAX, one thousand light years from earth. Jeff Bridges gives what is tantamount to a good supporting performance as the doctor trying to save his patient from his delusions to the detriment of his own family life.An excellent supporting cast give a fair and accurate portrayal of life in a Psychiatric institution. It is nice to see such a place portrayed without the need to show the usual heavy-handed orderlies manhandling patients and uncaring nurses injecting patients with tranquillisers at the first sign of trouble.The film opens with the character Prot helping a woman who has been attacked in a train station. From that opening scene Spacey gives Prot an unearthly quality. From the childlike innocence of each new discovery the audience travels the journey with him. Spacey's Prot is smug, occasionally arrogant and almost Christ-like but his effect on his fellow patients is what captures the imagination. It's a funny, engrossing yet poignant film, which leaves you feeling both charmed and horrified.</fullReview>

		<date>2002-04-09</date>
		<username>Caps Fan</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>A Thoughtful and Thought-Provoking Movie</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>As an actor, Kevin Spacey is not to everyone's taste. His understated style can seem samey and smug. Whether or not that criticism is true, such a style is perfect for this film.Our story begins and ends intriguingly. Spacey plays a being calling himself Prot (pronounced "Prote") who appears out of nowhere in the form of a man at Grand Central Station and is taken from there to a mental institution ? because he claims to come from another planet, the name of which gives the film its title. While at the Manhattan Psychiatric Institute, he interacts with, and in some cases helps, the other patients, and his therapist, Dr Mark Powell (Jeff Bridges).There are good scenes throughout the film. My own favorites are when Prot is able to out-think some professional astronomers at their own game. Later, he predicts that a blue bird will appear to delight his fellow patients. A blue jay duly does appear, to the dismay of some of Dr Powell's colleagues who dismiss the patients' delight as mass hysteria.At the end, Prot disappears, sort of, leaving the other patients to live on and Dr Powell to ponder acting on some advice he gives. He does act on it, in a superbly understated scene that brings the film to a satisfying conclusion.Performances, not just Spacey's, are good. Of particular note are Jeff Bridges and, especially, David Patrick Kelly in a deep, credible performance as the obsessive compulsive Howie. The music, also understated (that word again!), is just perfect.The only serious weakness is that too many of the secondary characters, particularly Dr Powell's wife (Mary McCormack) and some of his colleagues at the hospital, are clichés.I first saw this on a plane. When it finished, I sat for half an hour or more thinking about what I'd seen. It still has that effect on me and I wish more films did.Recommended then.Rating: 8/10.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>Geoff (geoffski2000@yahoo.com)</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>A brilliant, thought provoking film</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Possible SpoilersAhh...another of the "nutter" movies I hear you say...We've had quite a number of them from One Flew Over The Cuckoo's Nest To Girl, Interrupted and A Beautiful Mind. Whilst they were all brilliant in their own ways, and Cuckoo's Nest and Girl, Interrupted were also quite similar, K-Pax holds its own, and is less about the institution as it is a character play between Kevin Spacey (Prot) and Jeff Bridges (Dr. Mark Powell).The basic premise is this: At the beginning of the movie, Prot "appears" in the middle of grand central station and witnesses a bag snatch. When he tries to help the lady, the police question him, and then proceed to take him to belview (a mental institution) in the belief that he is mad. From here he ends up at a different institution under the care of Dr. Mark Powell, who sums up his character quite well with the quote to his secretary "Who is it this time? Jesus or Joan of Ark?". But, as you soon discover, Prot has a few surprises of his own, as he and Mark interact, both the doctor, and the viewer, are left wondering if it could actually be possible that he's telling the truth, and that he's really from K-Pax.The acting in this film is second to none, with Kevin Spacey solidifying his position as an A+ actor, and Jeff Bridges proving that he has many a trick still up his sleeve.The longer that Prot stays, the more changes that start occuring in the psychiatric institute. The patients mental health improves. And Prot gives his views on life as it is in K-Pax.It is a movie of many levels. First it is a great character piece between two of the most exceptional actors around today. Secondly it is a movie about a psychiatric institution and how there is hope even for the most "hopeless" of cases, and that one should never give up. Thirdly, it is a movie to make you wonder...wonder about what other life forms there may be, and wonder if we could be talking to someone who is from somewhere else and not even know it.And the ending is one of the best i have seen from a mainstream hollywood picture in a long time, as you are left to discover for yourself what the truth is, without having it wrapped up for you by the picture.All in all, K-Pax is a brilliant film that i would highly reccommend to everyone. See it now!</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>An emotionally enthralling masterpiece with a message for all of us</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Dr. Michael Powell, a respected psychiatrist working a the Psychiatric Institute of Manhattan, is confronted with the most difficult case of his career: A man, who calls himself Prot, claims to have come from K-PAX, a planet revolving around the binary stars Agape and Satori in the Lyra constellation. Dr. Powell approaches the case by trying to confront with the holes in his made-up world - which he doesn´t find, even with the help of a befriended astronomer. Could he really be an alien?Kevin Spacey (Prot) shows (again) that he is to be counted among the most excellent actors ever. Note, that this movie is not set in some kind of sci-fi world, it´s supposed to be the real world, in which you would laugh at somebody who claims to have just arrived from a planet a 1000 lightyears away - and in which such a person would be where Prot has to go to, a psychiatric hospital. A sane among the insane, both intellectually and emotionally above the things that happen around him and yet with a extraordinary capability of empathy - a difficult character that is perfectly and convincingly portrayed by Spacey. Jeff Bridges as Dr. Powell did excellent as well, though K-PAX is no vehicle of displaying Bridges' - top-notch - acting talents due to his limited on-screen presence.Don´t think, the core of the story is just an insane guy or an alien, it´s much more than that: It´s an exploration of the depths of human social life. It will leave you thinking about what you think is the essence of life - and that is what makes this movie a rare gem.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Kevin Spacey beams down another winner worth catching in the theatre...</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Once again Kevin Spacey delivers a terrific performance, this time as the likeable "alien" Prot in Iain Softley's("Hackers") new film, "K-PAX". Like a cross between "One Flew Over The Cuckoo's Nest" and "Starman", this movie has a great "magical" feel to it and actually challenges the viewer to come to his/her own conclusions about the sanity of Prot and what the ending actually means.The many thought-provoking topics find its way into the genre-hopping script and it seems to work pretty well. While not the most fast-paced movie out there, the story unfolds in such a way that the viewer is not bored easily.Although it has been called "deceptive filmmaking", I'd like to think of it as creative. The story almost comes off as a not-so-creepy "Twilight Zone" episode. It questions many basic theories of family, life, and doubt in beliefs. The emotions cover hope to despair and everything in between. It makes you ask, "What if?" on many different topics, not just the alien aspect."K-PAX" is a definite crowd-pleaser. This is definitely worth catching in the theater, especially if you're a big fan of Spacey or Bridges. This is, in fact, probably one of the more intriguing films to come out this year.</fullReview>

	<review>
		<date>2001-11-20</date>
		<username>Chris Brown (chrisbrown6453@hotmail.com)</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>A true must see.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>As theatergoers leave the auditorium, the same puzzled look appears on everyone's face. "What did that ending mean?" "What do you think happened?" In order to enjoy K-Pax, you must be willing to suspend disbelief for a few hours and leave your cynicism behind. Screenwriter Charles Leavitt takes you on a fantastic journey. The ending isn't packaged and sealed like most cinematic endeavors. It is left without masking tape to fill in the holes.Kevin Spacey plays Prot, a produce eating being from the planet K-Pax, who is sent to Dr. Mark Powell (Jeff Bridges), for psychiatric help. He claims that the planet is 1000 light-years away in the constellation Lyra. He explains that he is merely a visitor to this "BA-3 planet", a planet in its primitive stages of evolution with a question mark for a future. After many conversations with Prot, Dr. Mark Powell struggles with the truth behind the tale. Prot tells us that there are no families on K-Pax, no wives, and giving birth is more painful and hideous than any human will ever imagine. Prot knows information about astronomy that only the top astronomers in the world are privy to. Prot baffles everyone but Dr. Powell, who makes it his mission to find out the real story behind the man in the sunglasses.Originally a role for Will Smith, Kevin Spacey first received the script for the part of the psychiatrist. After reviewing it, Spacey didn't connect with the psychiatrist character as much as he did with Prot. Three years later, the movie is out and Spacey is our alien. Spacey is just as mysterious in real life as he is in his movies. He always plays a character with a certain tick that tocks to a different clock. Nevertheless, with his sly grin and sweet as a puppy demeanor, he will remain on the top-ten list of the most brilliant actors in Hollywood today. This movie touches upon many issues and themes that face many families. For Dr. Powell, we see that he neglects his family and is constantly on a non-stop work schedule. He is even reluctant to invite his son from his first marriage to visit him. In an interview with Jeff Bridges, he states that the movie helps to make you realize that love and families are what get you through rough spots in life and his character is at constant conflict with this notion. Dr. Powell's wife, Rachel (Mary McCormack), shows that love when she sits by her husband's side in a wonderful scene before the climax of the movie full of Chinese food and compassion.The one thing this movie lacks is originality. Much of this comes from the supporting cast filled with the cliché asylum whack jobs. They are the same in every movie. One with a nervous twitch, the other one who doesn't talk, another one who says that everyone in the room stinks and, of course, the man dressed in sterile garb with gloves and a face mask who dares not touch anything in fear of catching a disease. We've all seen these characters before. It's time we throw them away and find a new batch.Regardless, the team of Bridges and Spacey is incredibly strong. Their energies coincide well in a scene, constantly feeding off one another to create a fantastic pace. This movie is a "must see" by me.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>Christine Ewerdt</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Another Oscar worthy performance by Kevin Spacey! MUST SEE!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Starring Kevin Spacey (as Prot), Lloyd Bridges (as Dr. Mark Powell) and set in New York City, `K-PAX' has all the ear markings of an Oscar worthy film.Prot makes his first appearance at a NY subway station. A woman is mugged; he approaches her to offer help, but, instead is questioned by the police for possible involvement. During their brief interrogation, Prot tells them he is from K-PAX. He is immediately taken to a local mental institution for evaluation under suspicion of a hallucinogenic drug.Dr. Powell is assigned to Prot's case. With the thousands of cases he has dealt with throughout his career, he naturally dismisses the possibility that Prot could be from K-PAX. However, after seeing Prot's interaction with the other mental patients, the manner in which they respond to him, and the methods Prot uses to help them Dr. Powell begins to wonder if Prot is really from our world or another. Prot has amazing abilities: He is able to see ultraviolet rays, he possesses knowledge of our universe that is known to few, he can communicate with animals to name but a few.The movie focuses around Dr. Powell's desire to find out who Prot really is and where he comes from. We're led on an amazing path of discovery into the life of Prot and the people he has encountered during his stay on earth. What Dr. Powell discovers shocks not only him, but his colleagues and family members as well.Go to this movie with high expectations. You won't be disappointed.</fullReview>
	</review>

(I'll try and be "spoiler free" here, sticking to moments seen in the trailers).Some comments surround the technical aspects of Prot's role. Sure, he does some impressive technical things in the planetarium. But, then, we're brought back to earth, if you will, by the next scene. The story could have easily become a chase movie, with Jeff Bridges trying to protect Prot from being taken away by "men in black" intent on discovering what he was all about. That's basically the E.T. story. And "Starman", too, which Jeff Bridges has already done once.They chose to go here with more of a "Miracle on 34th Street" approach: is he Santa / is he an alien? So I think they downplayed the technology stuff. Maybe not enough, but I think the audience expected to see some magic to make the question plausible. Is it over done? Yes, I'd have to agree it is. But, I'd bet that during the movie most are sufficently distracted by the story that these questions didn't come up. At least it's no "Planet of the Apes" when it comes to glaring plot holes.Very good acting all around and you could tell this cast had a great time making this film.</fullReview>

		<username>Paul (freenhim@home.com)</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>The best film I've seen all year--a truly well-written movie.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I haven't seen a movie of this caliber all year. The best reviews of this movie don't do it justice and the plot is both realistic and enthralling. Unlike so many other movies set in mental institutions, K-PAX really keeps moving and holds the viewer's interest. But most impressive is the lack of constant foul language and the need to portray unrealistic violence and rebellion in the hospital. Overall I rate this movie a 9 out of 10.The movies I rank in this category are only a few--"Air Force One," "Rainman," "A River Runs Through It," just to name a few others. The portrayal of human emotions is well-thought out and the movie doesn't over do it. The basic premise of the movie is that Kevin Spacey, playing the character "Prot," is an extraterrestrial being from the planet K-PAX located 1000 light-years away from Earth. No one has seen him arrive and he seems to have no family, no home, no identity. As the plot unfolds, his uncanny grasp of facts and knowledge pertaining to the planet from which he originates begins to convince his doctor and other patients that he is telling the truth. What happens from there is a wonderful theme of human emotions, love of others, and an undiscerning care for friends and strangers alike. This movie was not a tearjerker or full of romantic sappiness, but it did lend a new perspective on life and living it to the fullest. And the plot kept you dying to find out what would happen next. As I said before, I rank it as one of the best movies I have ever seen and I think you will enjoy it, too.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Interesting, enjoyable film.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>K-PAX is a enjoyable, thought provoking movie. Kevin Spacey plays a man who might be an alien, or he might be insane. Jeff Bridges plays the doctor whose job it is to cure Spacey of his delusions. Every scene between these two great actors is perfect. They have interesting, intelligent conversations, so much more thought provoking than most mainstream films. The problems with K-PAX lie in the subplots. I am so tired of seeing men's wives in movies whine about how their husbands are never home. It's annoying. Cut out every scene with Bridge's wife whining and the movie is much better. The other patients in the mental ward with Spacey are cookie cutter characters. These are the same people we have met in every mental ward since ONE FLEW OVER THE CUCKOO'S NEST. Cut down on those scenes. Despite these flaws, K-PAX is still a very good movie. Spacey and Bridges are perfect. They have fun playing off each other. The ending is sure to confuse some people (I know one guy I work with told me he thought K-PAX sucked after I told him to go see it, because he didn't get the ending). The ending is the type of ending I love. It lets the audience decided what to think. I wish more movies trusted their audience as much as K-PAX does.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>A Toned Down Sci-Fi That Speaks To Our Souls</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>K-Pax can be compared arguably to Miracle On 34th Street (is he Santa/an Alien ?) The treatment of the film is mushy and more suited for the romantic similar to our other favorite little alien, E.T.Its a story about a relationship between two beings.. one who may/or may not be from 1000 light years away.I think the most important thing is not to get hung up on whether Prot (Kevin Spacey's character) is from K-Pax or not. One of the films most important lessons is that we all inherently have the abilities to help or heal ourselves. We just have to believe in it enough. That we need to open our mindset to possibilities that we haven't thought about. And isn't that what sci-fi is all about ?The second key message is that if we get second chances to redo our relationships, to try harder to reach the people we love and should reach, then we should do it. Not only that, but we allow more time to spend with them because the work will always be there.I took these messages to heart especially in these turbulent times where somebody we take for granted to be there day in day, will not be.Like Curly's (in City Slickers) one answer to life which is whatever it means to you, K-Pax's ending is whatever it means to you (Stop reading here if you dont want the spoiler or my interpretation). In my eyes, Prot went searching for someone to take care of his friend Robert Proctor, assumed his body to do so. After his long search, he finally found someone (Jeff Bridges) that he could entrust the care of his friend to. Someone who wouldn't just roll him into a corner and stick IVs into him just to keep him alive. And when he found the person for the job, he went home.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>You won't have all the answers but that's the point!!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I keep hearing people saying that they didn't understand the ending or that they waited the whole movie to find out the truth about Prot and then were disappointed in the end. This movie is meant to parallel real life, there are mysteries that we will never know for sure the answer to. This is what makes life interesting! If we knew all the answers then we would stop wondering and when that happens then aren't we basically dead? This movie was so original in that it didn't do the typical Hollywood thing of telling all the little "children" (viewers) in the end how things are. We are left to make up our own mind. And that is what we need more of today, people using there own minds instead of waiting for an answer to be given to them. I guess you've gathered by now that I loved this movie! I thought Kevin Spacey was excellent. Some viewers I guess cannot handle knowing that it is possible for a grown man to have an emotional outburst of pain ... when I went to see this movie, a girl actually laughed hysterically at this very scene. Are people so closed that they have to laugh to hide the fact that they might be affected by this type of emotion! The only thing and it's a small thing that bugged me in this movie was the very "Hollywood" portrayal of a mental institution. I don't want to sound cruel but I don't think that in real life that all the people in a mental hospital would be so easily loveable with just a few laughable quirks. I am sure it is much more complicated then that. This movie has it all, humour, drama, mystery and a mind opening question that you the viewer is left to decide. Viewers should feel gratitude to the makers of this movie for not assuming that we are so simple minded that we need a Hollywood movie to answer all of our questions in life. If you want to be left with something to think about and also be entertained, go see this movie!!</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Another Oscar for Spacey, please!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>This film is beautiful; one of those rare treats in Hollywood. Full of intelligence, wit, compassion, philosophy. It doesn't talk down to its audience, and it stars the one actor most perfectly suited to such a role: Kevin Spacey. This man just keeps getting better and better!Moreover, the ending is another big surprise. In an entertainment environment where I've gotten used to unhappy endings, violence, pessimism, and degradation of every description, this film isn't afraid to keep bringing you back to the sheer joy and wonder of life right to the last minute. It's full of hope without being cheesy, and thrives on the strength of a great story and brilliant acting uncluttered by mind-bending visual effects, a grating soundtrack (the music is lush and gorgeous), or mile-a-minute TV-commercial type editing, yet it still manages to look completely hip. This is science fiction with a human face, something we don't get to see nearly enough of.</fullReview>

I loved the symbolism, I loved the technical stuff, I just plain loved this movie period. Let's start with the plot. It was enticingly interesting, and most importantly, very different and original (I thought). The best thing about it, however, was not it's character development, it's witty dialogue, or it's techno babble, but the fact that it left so much open to interpretation. This is a movie that makes you think, that makes you "look at the world differently." It doesn't cram things down your throat for you to regurgitate later, but it lets you take it all in, and digest it over time- coming to your own conclusions. As for the cinematography- fabulous! It was almost as if you could feel the light on your face through the screen. There are so many interesting angles, so many manipulations, rainbows, interesting close-ups, different view-points, fresh takes on what we so often take for granted. Simply wonderful. Then there is the acting! Kevin Spacey, you are a god! Such emotion, such passion. You can tell these actors really cared about their characters and really wanted to do them justice. (I think I've found a new role model for my acting goals.) This movie is a definite winner- whether you like your movies mysterious, sci-fi, fantasy-minded, or dramatic, this movie has it all. Don't miss it.</fullReview>

	<review>
		<date>2001-10-28</date>
		<username>dreammuffin</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Just what the doctor ordered.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>The world is in need of a cogent meditation on dealing with grief in our troubled times. In "K-Pax" director Iain Softly, Kevin Spacey, Jeff Bridges and friends do a superior job in dolling out emotions that make your heart melt and your eyes tear.The mind is as activated as the heart in "K-Pax", as the viewer is taken on a mental roller-coaster ride from one version of reality to the next. You are lead to believe one thing about Prot; Kevin Spacey's unearthly mental patient; then another. Most movies only have one or two twists, "K-Pax" has at least three. My mind moving all over the place, I wasn't sure how it was going to end until it did. I assure you, however, that the ending is as deeply satisfying as it is sad.Mr. Bridges gives such a subtle, unaffected performance as a psychiatrist with communication issues he is sure to be jilted by the Academy again this year. (Time to play a cross-dresser.) And Mr. Spacey,...is Kevin Spacey. (It's hard to give the two-time Oscar winning champ a better compliment.) But I have to give props to the bit players in this non-rock-opera. The circus of characters that populate the psychiatric facility are incredibly well drawn out and well acted, I'm sure any one of them could carry a whole movie by themselves. I also enjoyed the bevy of Doctors that Prot was taken to meet. The family scenes fell flat however and I wish I could have gotten more of a love vibe from the Dr. and his wife and children, but that didn't retract form my overall positive feelings generated from this fine film.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>Great film, worth your time</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I was able to see an advance screening of K-PAX at my college. A free Sneak Preview is always good, but this time we had the added bonus that we actually saw a damn good movie.[MILD SPOILERS] Kevin Spacey impresses me yet again here with his portrayal of the character Prot. The acting is so good that at the end of the film, you can honestly question yourself whether he really is an alien, or merely a deranged mental patient. It is almost entirely to the credit of Spacey's interpretation of Prot that allows you to not be sure of the 'right' answer.Playing Prot's straight man is Jeff Bridges, as the psychiatrist assigned to help Prot realize that he is a human being. Bridges character of Mark is as down-to-earth as you can get, and a very comfortable opposition to the more 'out there' character of Prot.Perhaps the best part of the film is how it is all tied together, without strictly giving an answer. Seemingly un-important details near the beginning are given relevance near the end, and yet the big question of "Is he or isn't he?" is left up to the imagination of the movie-goer.In summary, K-PAX is well worth your time, and will be nominated for at least a few Oscars when the time comes, I'm sure.</fullReview>

The story seemed to have what I considered a contrived ending. Watching it once again now, I have a wiser and deeper appreciation for the character of Prot, the shattered Robert Porter who subsumed his identity following the trauma of losing his family and exacting a revenge totally inimical to his true nature. Kevin Spacey is eerily brilliant in his portrayal of Prot, with a calmness of spirit and purpose that comes across as not only realistic, but oddly comical when the situation calls for it.All that considered, one still requires a certain leap of faith to make the picture work. I'm thinking here of Prot's ability to precisely pin point the location of K-Pax to the satisfaction of the scientists. There's no way to explain a million to one shot like that in the course of every day events. And of course, there's no way to explain the disappearance of Bess. Yet, the three tasks given Howie (David Patrick Kelly) were a wonderful sub-text to carry the picture forward, and brilliant in it's simplicity. Particularly that last one - 'stay here and be prepared for anything'. Isn't that the best advice any one of us can have?</fullReview>

		<username>Martin Bradley (MOscarbradley@aol.com)</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>A very pleasant surprise with two terrific performances</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Few actors can play off-the-wall quite as well as Kevin Spacey. On the one hand he's the most 'normal' looking of actors but then there is always that smile that says 'I know more than you do', the intonation in the voice that says 'I have a secret' and eyes that seem to look right through you. So when in this movie he says he's an alien from the Planet K-Pax you don't rush to disbelieve him; at least the psychiatrist assigned to his case doesn't. The premise is, of course, totally ludicrous yet Iain Softley's film is wholly convincing. I mean, if Kevin Spacey told me I was an alien from the Planet K-Pax I'd probably believe him.This is a classy entertainment, in some respects not too far removed from "One Flew Over the Cuckoo's Nest" with Spacey as a kind of Randall P. McMurphy figure whose influence on his fellow patients is considerably more benign and beneficial than that of the doctor's treating them, but in place of Nurse Ratchid we have Jeff Bridges' kindly psychiatrist, and Bridges is superb. There is something wonderfully grounded about him. He is highly intelligent and utterly anchored at the same time, the smart, likable boy-next-door who's made good.Ultimately however it is Spacey's film. It's a genuine tour-de-force, taking a real actor's delight in knowing just how good he is and just how good his material is. He ups the ante on what is already a first-rate film and if the final revelations err a little too much on the predictable at least the journey to them is worthwhile and finally very moving.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>shoplifter</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>"I travel light"</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Kevin Spacey plays a man who is a patient at a psychiatric hospital in New York City and who claims to be from another planet. In the research they did in several mental institutions, in order to make this movie, one of the questions Spacey would ask the staff was if they had anybody there who believed they come from another planet. It seemed that this belief was not uncommon because their answer would be there were like a dozen of them believers. Jeff Bridges plays the psychiatrist, whose job it is to try to determin whether he is a patient who is suffering from some kind of amnesia, whether he's had some kind of trauma, whether he's a multiple personality, delusional, exceptional ... On some level the film is about what happens when you encounter a stranger who has some rather extraordinary effect on all the other people around him. It is also a mystery where it keeps going back and forth between this question of "is he?" or "isn't he?", "could he be?", "possibly?", "no not?". It manages to walk this fine line right up to the end of the film. When doctors or people of science are looking at the facts up front and there's nothing to indicate the thing that the're worried about, for instance suppose someone goes in and they suffer from extreme headachs all the time and you're trying to find some evidence of that but there's nothing to prove that there should be this thing. It turns the situation very mysterious. At first, when Prot says he is an alien from the planet K-PAX, they attribute it to to some kind of psychosis or memory loss, but there's nothing to indicate that. So it rouses the doctors up and it peeks their curiosity because he has the facts of the world where he comes from.This movie is not about science fiction but about the science of humanity. What do we believe is true and what don't we believe is true? How do we begin to understand things that we don't see and things we don't comprehend? How do we categorize things in order to feel safe?</fullReview>
	</review>

His unassuming nature as an otherworlder is genius, and his facial expressions speak volumes and they share a level of honesty not often seen in movies (my opinion, of course). His mannerisms in dealing with people (of this planet) are short, sweet, to the point, and they evince a way of thinking I only wish I could engender more often: Look at the things you have and try to enjoy life more; remember that work is only how you make a living, and family is all-important. His casual witticisms turn out to be lessons in life. So often movies start with a premise they want to get across, and they struggle through two hours trying to get a single point across (if there is one to start with). Kevin in K-PAX gets some of the most basic ideas across without even trying, and you actually REMEMBER them! (example: "Every being in the universe knows right from wrong, Mark."). One of my most favorite scenes in the move is is when he talks to and plays with Dr. Powell's dog, Shasta. His actions are so genuine and it just looks like he's having a great time playing with this dog!! There are just so many excellent moments in K-PAXIf I had only one thing to say about this movie, it would be simply to thank Kevin Spacey for the experience. Of the 700 movies in our collection at home, there are only two that I consider to be a true experience. This is one of them.</fullReview>

The visuals with light is mesmerizing, Iain Softly the director did a wonderful job, especially with the lighting, casting and choice of composer for the music. Edward Shearmuir is a great composer. His music blends so well with the abstract of the story line, intensifies at the appropriate tense scenes and just does the job. The story is very cleverly crafted to keep the viewer guessing right until the end and, even then, no definitive answer is given. However I would like to think there are enough clues and signs as the tale unfolds to point to the more extraordinary possibility as being the case. At the end of the day, if aliens really did travel to our planet from great distances, they could only do so by means we cannot even begin to comprehend. Once here, they are more likely to take form or a host which allows them to exist among us, than arrive in V style spaceships.There is a lot to learn from this film (which, although not as detailed as the book, is better that the book for mystery and realism). I loved this film from the start (even the music is excellent); it is a slow, unfolding mystery that manages to install different emotions and feelings within the audience. You don't have to like Sci-Fi to enjoy this film - there is something for everyone in it, and a lot to learn and think about. What we do in life, how we treat people and how we live our lives is the central theme for me. If someone is mad, does that make them less of a person? Does science, medical test and medication have all the answers? Happiness is a road, it is happening now, trap the spark and hold it there, you won't be disappointed. This provoking film is one that will stay with you for a long time after seeing it and is even better the second time.Overall rating: 9 out of 10.</fullReview>

Along with a ethereal sound track and melody, this nicely off-balance and emotionally touching movie has the audience face up to innocence and the important matters of living using mental health conditions as a backdrop that is respectively acted and performed in a less harsh and dramatic presentation and with perhaps even more redeeming uplifting value than the sci fi classic Twelve Monkeys (1996) or the murder mystery of Shutter Island (2010).</fullReview>

One, a young Black woman, Bess, either won't or cannot talk through much of the story, due to the traumatic loss of her home in a fire. She has a few lines later on, but it isn't so much the dialog that grabs you. It is the realization at the end that she has somehow overcome her inner demons. All the patients look into her empty room, bed all made neatly. One says something to the effect that "She has gone to K-Pax". That moment, for me, crowned the story. But it does not diminish the rest of the story at all. Rather it validates every minute of the movie. Even though we find out at the end what we already knew, that Prot is just as human as the rest of us......you will not be able to keep from wishing Prot well on his trip back to K-Pax!</fullReview>

The more the movie progresses the more it seems like either could be true. The ability he has to map where his planet is where no human has the ability dumbfounds experts. Kevin Spacey shows his abilities as an actor by acting cool and logical as Prot one scene and then can easily switch to a more tormented personality next. He makes both alter egos believable and makes us the viewer with a more difficult job of trying to figure out which he really is. We then are left with Jeff who is excellent and becomes obsessed with trying to find out who the real Prot is. K-Pax shows us that life is contains of infinite possibilities, some of them are know others remain a mystery. With the vast unknown who are we to say what exists or what is possible. Who are we to say what exists or even what is certain. Both of these are looked into in a story in a individuals journey that is both strange and dramatic that challenges ones logic. All of these unanswered questions challenge Dr. Powell's nature. Powell has to know the truth get cant get it out of his mind and with the truth can set his own mind free. With this being a very thought provoking film that continues to challenge us by keeping the mystery on who the real Prot is and reflecting on what is possible. This is a must see movie.</fullReview>

When a new patient is brought to a mental institution claiming to be an inhabitant of a planet called K-PAX, the hospital seems just the place for him. Yet, except for certain otherworldly abilities, the "alien," he, appears to be perfectly sane. In taped therapy sessions he is asked about life on K-PAX - its lifestyle, principles, foods, language. He paints a consistent and credible portrait of a glorious utopia painfully unlike our own and yet so possible, could we only erase from human nature its greed and cruelty. It becomes easy, even desirable, to believe in his identity and homeland. But he insists that he must return home. As his announced date of "departure" approaches, staff and patients alike are thrown into turmoil: If he is mad, what will happen when the fateful day arrives? If K-PAX is for real...please, may they come along too?</fullReview>

		<date>2003-03-16</date>
		<username>(DAVEYFOO@HOTMAIL.COM)</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>PERCEPTION</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>If you have not seen the film then dont read on because there are possible spoilers ahead.............. I have read the other postings about the film and the discussion over whether Prot was really an alien or just a mentally ill person. To me, the film was about perception. But, here is where it is very clever...its not just the perception of those who encounter Prot within the film but the audience as well. Like Mulholland drive, the audience is left with many questions. Was Prot an alien? Was he an alter ego of Kevin Porter, that by his very nature of being alien meant he did have to deal with the extreme emotions that Kevin would experience? After all, would an alien have any perception of emotions such as sadness or anger? Why was Bess chosen over the other guy who had the three tasks to complete...what was special about her? But more importantly, was the film about the Doctor helping Prot or the way Prot helped the Doctor? We are shown the facts yet there is still some doubt left and this is what makes K-PAX a great film. Many films lead the audience to a specific conclusion, which leaves little room for any discussion afterwards.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>home2bed</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>A nice way to pass a little time</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>You have probably seen every element of this film before. It seems to have been assembled out of spare parts, but that does not make it bad -- just ordinary. Here is an unchallenging, very competently made story of a man who might be insane, and might be -- as he claims -- an alien. There is evidence for both possibilities, presented as a series of cliches. Try "The amazing knowledge that stuns scientists", which the scientists don't bother to follow up. Or what about "The gentle inmate who cheers up the other cute and interesting patients in the psychiatric ward". Or "The psychiatrist who takes the patient home to play with his children". Spacey and Bridges walk through the whole film virtually deadpan, Spacey mostly wearing dark glasses. Any two actors could have done an equal job, although Bridges looks somewhat too old and there has to be a little explanation of why his wife is so much younger. If you like gentle sci-fi, injury-free hospital dramas, and a film that does not rely on stunts, special effects or sex to keep it going, its a nice way to pass the time.</fullReview>

		<username>rdarlington</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>"I've got a light beam to catch"</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Great title, reminiscent of `THX 1138' from George Lucas. However, although this might sound like another science fiction movie - which initially put off my wife ? this is an earth-bound tale devoid of special effects. Kevin Space, as a character called Prot, is either a visitor from a planet called K-PAX who can travel faster than the speed of light or someone very seriously mentally ill with complex and detailed delusions. Assigned to find out is Jeff Bridges as Dr Mark Powell who ? on his own admission ? becomes too deeply involved in the mystery.Spacey, an actor with an ?otherworldliness' about him and a surname to match, is utterly believable as the benevolent and insightful alien with a consuming taste for fruit. Of course, Bridges has been here before and performs well as the doctor who often cares more about his patients than his family. He was himself a visitor from outer space in `Starman' and he was a psychiatrist again in `Vanilla Sky'. Indeed so well cast are the two that it's hard to imagine that originally Spacey was going to be the shrink and Will Smith was slated to be the spaceman.There are some good lines (`I've got a light beam to catch'), but unfortunately it all looks rather familiar. The idea of a man with seemingly magic powers was done in `Phenomenon' and the cathartic revelations in the psychiatrist's office is straight out of `The Prince Of Tides'. Although there is much sentimentally, the ending is uncharacteristically down-beat and ? unless you're like me and watch all the credits ? you'll miss a tiny scene at the very end of this particular rainbow.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>I have been waiting for a long time...</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>...for this movie. And when it finally came I was thrilled. Though, now, when I've seen it I might have had too high hopes. Not that the movie wasn't good - because it was - but it could have been better.I read the book several years ago. My mum gave it to me since she liked PROT and she thought that I and him had some similarities. In many ways we probably do. The book made me dream of the world of K-PAX and I really wanted to go there. "Pick me...", I remember I once said, as everyone else probably did when reading the novel.What bothers me most about the film though, is not the adaption itself, since it follows the book much better than any adaption ever has done before it. This is a good thing. However, bits and pieces are missing, and when leaving the theater I understand what it is that I miss the most: it is the politics of K-PAX! K-PAX is in the novel an anarcho-syndicalistic world in its most pure essence. It is a world without money, without rules, without "law and lawyers" as PROT states it. But it is still a world in peace.I remember when I read it that I said to myself that "this can't work in the US". And when watching the movie, I understand that it didn't. Actually, almost everything of the message in the book is erased! K-PAX is a lovely world - but what if we tried to re-create it here on Earth? Well, I guess the producers didn't want to take a risk developing a too socialstic idea on the screen.Gene Brewer's ideas are not only interesting. To me the ideas of the K-PAX-world is something we should try to create. If I said that to the capitalistic forces of the world I would be stoned to death. I do understand though, that an American film with these points couldn't be made in the world today. K-PAX, the REAL K-PAX-story (I mean the book) is light-years ahead of itself.But hey, we are only a class B-3 planet, so what do we know about the world?K-PAX is a very good movie. It is more sad than I thought it would be, but PROT is as nice and thoughtful that I always has visioned him. Kevin Spacey does a wonderful, maybe his best, performance. Jeff Bridges is also good, and it is a wise, if not strange choice, to cast him as the doctor when thinking of that he made STARMAN in 1984.PROT is yet an alien that is put in the line of Starman, E.T. and the rest of the friendly aliens from Hollywood. However, PROT has a message to us earthlings that the others didn't really have. You won't get this message by watching the movie; no, then you'd only get a good time. But if you read the book when you get home, then you will know what PROT really had to say.My vote: 7 of 10.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>good performances-- generic material</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>potential spoilers!!!!!K-Pax is undoubtedly a waste of the formidable acting chops of both Spacy and Bridges. Both men turn in subtle performances, peppered with believable vocal and physical mannerisms. The subject matter, however leaves alot to be desired. The fundamental flaw is that the film asks us to care about the Jeff Bridges character's family relationship without developing these characters at al. Neither the children or his wife are given any voice, nor is the reason for their familial strife explored futher than simply saying that Bridges is a "workaholic". Such a generic explanation is fine as backstory, but it cannot be used as the primary motivation for a protagonist's actIONSSPOILERS ALERT!!!!Nowhere in te film is this more evident than in the relationship between Bridges and his estranged son. This relationship is dismissed with the explanation that " they don't talk." For one t have any emotional investment in their reunion, we must have a more significant esxplanation than this. This film purports to explore the worldly by means of the supernatural, but it merely glosses over the most fundamentally human elements of the film.An attempt at Capraesque schmaltz that lacke the social insight and commentary to acchieve that level of quality. A predictable, dull, and simplistic film. Bridges and Spacey wasted their time on this rubbish, but that doesn't mean you have to.</fullReview>

	<review>
		<date>2001-12-01</date>
		<username>Aussie Stud</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Kevin Spacey shines in a fairy-tale "PATCH ADAMS" meets "E.T."</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Can Kevin Spacey do no wrong? Save for perhaps his little foible, "THE BIG KAHUNA", Spacey proves he can just about turn any role into a delightful character that viewers can somehow connect with and enjoy.In this particular story, "K-PAX" is the name of Kevin Spacey's home planet, and it is where he must return to on July 27th unless Jeff Bridges can convince him not to otherwise.Spacey plays, "Prot" (pronounced like 'boat'), a peculiar kind-hearted gentleman dressed in 'everyman's clothes' who enters the film at a crowded train station in New York and helps a lady off the floor who has just been mugged. Police officers arriving on the scene mistake Prot for the offender and after a brief questioning session, decide that something is missing 'upstairs' in his head and have him committed to a psychiatric ward and in particular to Jeff Bridges' care.Jeff Bridges is a highly over-looked esteemed actor. I've felt that his last few films (especially ones such as "THE CONTENDER" and "ARLINGTON ROAD") were some extraordinary high-lights of his career. In "K-PAX" he portrays Mark Powell, a psychiatrist who seems to be stuck in a rut with the same patients and their continuous never-ending problems. The patients at this institution aren't particularly dangerous, not really to anyone else but themselves. When Powell is introduced to Prot, we witness a strange connection between Psychiatrist and Patient that was non-existent with his other subjects.Prot explains to Powell that his is from the planet K-Pax and that he must return on July 27. What has he been doing here this whole time? What was his mission on Earth? Why does he have to go back? These are answers that only you will discover IF you see the movie.Prot's only objective in this film is that when he returns to K-Pax, he may only take one person with him. Unlike 1998's cliche'-driven tissue-in-your-hand 'fest "PATCH ADAMS", this film tries to avoid the saccharine-sweet route by having the patients actually believe in something and in doing so, making themselves a better person - Exactly, you won't find Kevin Spacey singing "Blue Skies" to the other patients or wearing a red clown's nose to make the children laugh. Prot helps turns the patients' lives around in offering them something that delivers hope, and it is not long before everyone suddenly wants to go to K-Pax.Powell is fascinated by Prot. You can tell that he wants to believe him and that this isn't just some usual babble he hears every day from his other patients. Prot has an aura of mystery around him and he is determined to discover literally down to the core, who and perhaps what, Prot exactly is.Several amusing scenes have Prot conversing with Powell's family dog and Prot mapping out the exact orbital system of the solar system he is from to a group of highly-educated Astronomers to prove that he isn't what Powell would describe as the case of a 'idiot savant'. But it is Prot's fascination with fresh produce that is one of his character high-lights.Several deeply disturbing scenes would include Powell engaging in psycho-therapeutic hypnotic sessions with Prot in order to gain further information about his past, and the final pieces of the puzzle that Powell will discover that fall into place will make this film something that a child may not want to see.Overall, I felt that "K-PAX" was heart-warming, touching and very smart in how it all falls into place. While there are certainly many plot holes to question, the film's conclusion will definitely have you talking it over in great detail with the person you just saw it with. Save for one curse word, I highly enjoyed this film and I would recommend it to just about everyone who isn't committed to seeing a film that involves things getting blown up and people getting shot.MY RATING: 9 'STARS' out of 10!</fullReview>
	</review>
	<review>

		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Not what I was expecting.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>While watching the preview of this movie, I imagined an insightful Sci-Fi work that parallels such great movies like Contact or the Arrival. But this movie was not exactly what I was hoping for. Spoiler: As expected, the movie's plot line dangles between "so, is he from outer space or not," much like in Contact, where the question was "so, did she really go or not" to keep the audience interested. But, in Contact, the question was more significant in that her question involved the theological conflict between science and religion, the contests between the government and a nemesis billionaire, and the treachery of human selfishness. In contrast, Prot's influence never seeped out of the psychiatric ward. His "benevolence" was only felt by a small group of crazed people. This element alone makes "the question" in K-Pax less significant, and less exciting. Also, it was quite surprising that after Prot dramatically demonstrated his knowledge (perhaps the highest point in the entire more), which proved (at least to me) that he is from outer planets, that nothing was done about it (also seemed strange to me that they never asked Prot to simply get from one side of the room to the other side of the room in light speed, which could have proven his ability to travel faster than light). Maybe it was the philosophy of the writers to shy away from MIB or ID4 type of alien extravaganza, but I was expecting a whole new plot line after that point, something that would parallel the story line of the Arrival, where the "real" reason of why he is here is discovered (they also never made quite clear why he would come to Earth). My point is that the second half could have been much more exciting (and believable) than just watching Prot locked up in the ward, figuring out if he is telling the truce from hypnosis when the whole world could be changed by Prot's knowledge.  Maybe it was because I had a preconception of the movie, but I find myself not intellectually satisfied when the movie ended. This movie strikes me more like a "One Flew over Cuckoo's Nest" with a spaceman in it. Its not a bad movie. Just not as good as I had hoped. </fullReview>

		<shortDescription>It ain't over till....</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Once again, your patience and interest were rewarded. A scene inserted at the very end of the credits clarifies Dr. Powell (Jeff Bridges) response to Prot's (Kevin Spacey) final request. For those who didn't stay, you have another good reason to see K-PAX again.Need some other reasons? This deceptively simple allegory will peel like an onion revealing psychological, spiritual, political, scientific and comical layers. And the irony of Jeff Bridges (of ?Starman' fame) showing up on the other side of the intergalactic ? You've at least seen the teasers and know that Prot is a stranger in a strange land (Manhattan) with an unfathomable understanding of deep space and innocence to cut to the heart with simple questions. Dr. Powell is forced to question all he knows about treatment and family issues. The hospital administration and our political leaders should rethink what constitutes a threat to society. And our spiritual leaders need to rethink revelation (satori) and love (agape).This film begs for a sequel, leaving the Prot's future up in the air. He turns the tables on the doctors at the Psychiatric Institute Manhattan, brings patients to a new level of awareness through Zen-like tasks and bridges the communication between family and dog. This film begs - no demands ? us to read the book.Not since Memento (way back before 9/11) has a film succeeded in putting the audience into the shoes of the protagonist. Confused? You should be. Where is it written that a film should only make you feel good? What's wrong with one that challenges? After all, we are at an " early stage of evolution; future uncertain." Which leads me to a major message from K-PAX: sometimes the answers we seek are not as important as the questions we ask.So who is the real Starman? Next April, the Academy may give you their decision.</fullReview>

		<username>bryceh</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Interesting Movie...</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Out of all the movies I've seen dealing with alien life, this is by far one of the most interesting and well presented. Instead of having a character who is trying to hide his existance as an extraterrestrial, we have one who openly admits this, to such an extent that he is considered an insane human. Spacely's character Prot, answers all the traditional questions which one might ask an alien to prove that he isn't really human. Will some of his answers are obscure, I found them all quite satisfying. I'm glad the movie actually addressed such issues instead of leaving unsightly plotholes.*SPOILER WARNING* Lots of people seem to be bashing this movie for it's "You decide what happened" ending. My personal opinion is that this isn't the case. What I got from the story was that Prot's species had to somehow occupied a human's body in order to exist on earth, but the human would still be there, coexisting in the same body with the alien. Prot occupied and made friends with a human (forgot his name) in this way and visited often. On the night of the murder, this human broke down emotional and tried to kill himself. Prot managed to save the body but the man's mind was gone. At the end of the movie when Prot returns home, he leaves the body behind, asking the Dr to take care of it. Evidence that he was really alien is overwhelming. He could see ultraviolet light. He was able to diagram his solar system, which the world's top Astrologers couldn't do with the data they had. He disappeared from a high-security mental institution and reappeared days later. Finally, he was able to take one of the patients with him to K-PAX. So tell me, how could he not be alien. I got the impression that the director wasn't trying to hide the fact that he was an alien, especially considering all the hints and clues that were put in the movie. *END OF SPOILERS*Overall, K-PAX is a great movie which gives an interesting perspective on the issue of life on other planets. I recommend this movie and give it a 9 of 10.</fullReview>
